## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population dynamics / mathematical ecology
**Analysis**: The task models population growth rate dP_dt as a function of time t and current population P, directly placing it in population dynamics. The core physical relationship involves density-dependent processes, growth saturation, possible time-varying environmental factors, and nonlinear feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited intrinsic growth)
- Logistic differential equation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (self-limiting growth with carrying capacity c0/c1)
- Generalized logistic / Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (asymmetric density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (log-form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (relative growth rate decays linearly with log P)
- Linear density-dependent birth/death: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2 (general second-order polynomial
- Power-law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric growth, no fixed carrying capacity)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic in P with bistable thresholds)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * t)) (environment that improves or deteriorates linearly)
- Periodic forcing (seasonal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (seasonal breeding or harvesting superimposed on logistic growth)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (exponentially changing life-history conditions)
- von Bertalanffy-like growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic and catabolic terms)
- Sigmoidal with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) + c2 (constant addition mimics restocking or immigration)
- Rational saturation immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (Holling-type functional responses in harvested populations)
- Double saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 / (1 + c2 * P**c1) (Hill-type per capita growth rate)
- Exponential decay in density feedback: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (Ricker-like growth model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- A negative quadratic P**2 term (with positive linear P) signals logistic self-limitation and a finite carrying capacity.
- A cubic polynomial in P with two positive roots indicates an Allee effect and bistable population dynamics.
- Appearance of log(P) in the growth rate suggests Gompertz-type senescence or declining per capita growth with log density.
- Sinusoidal terms in t reflect seasonal forcing (periodic environmental fluctuations) imposed on baseline growth.
- A constant term independent of P represents external immigration, emigration, or constant harvesting pressure.
- Product of P and a time-dependent function (e.g., exp(c*t) or linear t) indicates a temporally changing per capita growth rate or environmental capacity.
- A power-law term P**c without quadratic feedback hints at allometric or scale-free growth laws (e.g., in body mass growth).
- Rational forms like P/(P+c) model saturating predation or harvesting with a handling time (functional response type II).
- Exponential of -P (e.g., exp(-c*P)) produces overcompensation dynamics, often seen in discrete-generation models adapted to continuous form.
- Additive combinations of birth and death terms as separate linear/nonlinear components signal mechanistic decomposition of vital rates.

I need to first simplify the Ground Truth expression to understand what functional form it takes.

**GT expression:**
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P^(1/3)
```

Let me expand this. Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511035054181695`, `d = 13.538092585698905`.

**First term:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`

Let me expand `(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)`:
= `-1 + P/d + P/b - P²/(bd)`
= `(P/b + P/d - 1) - P²/(bd)`

So first term = `a*P*(P/b + P/d - 1 - P²/(bd))`
= `a*(P²/b + P²/d - P - P³/(bd))`

**Second term:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P = a*(P - P²/d)`

**Third term:** `a*P^(1/3)`

**Combining all:**
= `a*P²/b + a*P²/d - a*P - a*P³/(bd) + a*P - a*P²/d + a*P^(1/3)`

Simplify:
- `-a*P + a*P` cancels
- `a*P²/d - a*P²/d` cancels

**GT = a*P^(1/3) + a*P²/b - a*P³/(bd)**

So GT = `a*P^(1/3) + (a/b)*P² - (a/(bd))*P³`

This is: **c*P^(1/3) + d*P² + e*P³** where c, d, e are constants.

Computing:
- Coefficient of P^(1/3): `a = 0.72136`
- Coefficient of P²: `a/b = 0.72136/6.6511 ≈ 0.10846`
- Coefficient of P³: `-a/(bd) = -0.72136/(6.6511*13.5381) ≈ -0.72136/90.057 ≈ -0.008010`

So **GT = c₀*P^(1/3) + c₁*P³ + c₂*P²** with specific constants, and **no dependence on t**.

Now I need to check which candidates can reduce to exactly `P^(1/3)*A + P³*B + P²*C` (with no other terms).

Let me go through each candidate:

**Candidates with only `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2`:**

**Candidates with `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2 + c3`:** (Candidate 77)

**Candidate 45:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2 + P²*c3 + P*c4 + c5` — set c4=0, c5=0, absorb c3 into c2. ✓ **MATCH**

**Candidate 44:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P³*c2 + P²*c3 + P²*c4 + P²*c5 + P*c6 + c7` — set c6=0, c7=0. ✓ **MATCH**

**Candidate 75:** Same structure as 44 but without P*c6. Set c6=0. ✓ **MATCH**

But the question is asking which candidates **mathematically equate** to the GT. But wait - is this really the intent? Let me re-read: "Your task is to verify which candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth."

With free constants, if I can set extra terms to zero, then almost everything matches. But I think the intent is more nuanced - the question is whether the functional FORM can represent the GT, not just by zeroing everything extra.

Actually, re-reading the rules: "You can assign ANY real number (including 0) to candidate constants." This explicitly allows zeroing. So yes, any candidate where the extra terms can be zeroed and the remaining terms match GT's form should be a MATCH.

But let me reconsider Candidate 24: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5*exp(P*c6)`. Set c6=0: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5`. Set c1=0. We have `P²*c0 + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5`. Set c2=1/3, c4=3: `P²*c0 + P^(1/3)*c3 + P³*c5`. ✓ **MATCH**

I was wrong earlier. Let me recheck Candidate 24. Yes, with c6=0, c1=0, c2=1/3, c4=3, this gives P²*c0 + P^(1/3)*c3 + P³*c5. **MATCH**

**Candidate 25 recheck:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P^c3*c4*sin(c5*t+c6) + c7*t/(P+c8)^5`

**Candidate 42 recheck:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3*exp(P*c4) + c5*log(P^c6*c7+1)`
Set c4=0: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c5*log(P^c6*c7+1)`. Set c5=0, c1=0: `P²*c0 + P^c2*c3`. Missing P³. Can we get P³? No other term available. **NO MATCH**

Actually wait - we could set c2=3 to get P³*c3, but then we lose P^(1/3). We need both P^(1/3) AND P³ simultaneously. With only one P^c term, we can only get one of them. **NO MATCH** confirmed.

**Candidate 85 recheck:** `P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3*log(P^c4*c5+1) + c6*sin(P*c7+c8)`

**Candidate 87 recheck:** Same issue - no P^(1/3) available. **NO MATCH**
